Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is a condition where breathing repeatedly stops and starts during sleep.
  It is caused by a blockage of the airway, usually when the soft tissue in the back of the throat collapses during sleep.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign tumor of the jawbone.
  Dentigerous cyst is a type of cyst that forms around the crown of an unerupted tooth.
  Orbital fracture is a break in one of the bones surrounding the eye.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition where the jaw joint is fused and movement is restricted.
  None of these conditions seem to be directly related to obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Therefore, the answer is None of the Above.

Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient had a myocardial infarction (heart attack) 2 weeks back.
  The lipid profile shows low HDL, high LDL, and high TG levels.
  The patient is at risk for further cardiovascular events.
  Statins are the preferred medication for reducing LDL levels.
  Fibrates are preferred for reducing TG levels and increasing HDL levels.
  Combination therapy with a statin and a fibrate may be considered in patients with high TG levels and low HDL levels.
  However, combination therapy increases the risk of side effects such as myopathy and rhabdomyolysis.
  Therefore, monotherapy with a statin or a fibrate is preferred.
  Option A (Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate) is not preferred due to the increased risk of side effects.
  Option B (Fenofibrate alone) may be considered to reduce TG levels and increase HDL levels.
  Option C (Rosuvastatin 10 mg) is preferred as it will reduce LDL levels and may also have a modest effect on increasing HDL levels.
  Option D (Atorvastatin 80 mg) is not preferred as it is associated with a higher risk of side effects compared to lower doses of statins.
  Therefore, the preferred option for this patient is C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg.
Action: Answer("C")

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Thought:
  The third ventricle is a narrow cavity located in the midline of the brain.
  It is bounded by the thalamus and hypothalamus on either side.
  The floor of the third ventricle is formed by the hypothalamus.
  The optic stalk and infundibulum are present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  The third nerve emerges from the midbrain and passes through the interpeduncular fossa, but it does not form a part of the floor of the third ventricle.
  The mammillary body is a pair of small round structures located on the undersurface of the brain.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Third nerve.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:

  The mammillary body is not present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Mammillary body.

Question: For which of the following is PPV-23 is most beneficial:
Choices:
  A: Cystic fibrosis patient
  B: Sickle cell anemia patient
  C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis
  D: Child less than 2 years
Response 0:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is a pneumococcal vaccine that protects against 23 types of pneumococcal bacteria.
  Cystic fibrosis patients are at a higher risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Sickle cell anemia patients are also at a higher risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis may benefit from the vaccine, but it is not the most beneficial group.
  Children less than 2 years old are usually given PCV-13 vaccine, which protects against 13 types of pneumococcal bacteria.
  Therefore, the most beneficial group for PPV-23 vaccine is either A or B.
Action: Answer("A or B")

  A: Primary hypothyrodism
  B: Pituitary tumor
  C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma
  D: TSH resistance

  Swelling of pituitary gland suggests a pituitary tumor.

  Therefore, the most likely diagnosis is a pituitary tumor.

Topic: Dental
Question: Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in
primary teeth because of:
Choices:
  A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young
  B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex
  C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth
  D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young
Response 0:
Thought:
  Pulpectomy and pulp capping are treatments for dental pulp.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that erupt in a child's mouth.
  Primary teeth have different characteristics compared to permanent teeth.
  Increased odontoblastic activity means that the pulp is more active in producing dentin.
  Increased blood supply means that the pulp is more likely to heal.
  Increased volume of pulp means that there is more pulp tissue to work with.
  Lesser amount of collagen fibres means that the pulp is more flexible and can adapt better to treatment.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Pulpectomy is the removal of the entire pulp from the pulp chamber and root canal of a tooth.
  Pulp capping is a dental procedure used to prevent the death of dental pulp after an exposure or near exposure, by placing a protective dressing over the pulp.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that develop in a child.
  The pulp of primary teeth is larger and has more blood supply than the pulp of permanent teeth.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Pulpectomy is a root canal treatment for primary teeth.
  Pulp capping is a procedure to treat a small area of decay in a tooth.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that erupt in children.
  Primary teeth have different characteristics than permanent teeth.
  The answer should explain why pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth.
  Option A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young - Odontoblasts are cells that form dentin. Increased odontoblastic activity means that more dentin can be formed. This could be a reason why pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth.
  Option B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex - Blood supply is important for healing. However, this option does not explain why pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth.
  Option C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth - This option is not correct. Primary teeth have less pulp volume than permanent teeth.
  Option D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young - Collagen fibres are important for the strength of the tooth. This option does not explain why pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth.
  
  Therefore, the answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Thought: 
  Pulpectomy is the removal of the entire pulp from the root canal, while pulp capping is the placement of a medicament over the exposed pulp to stimulate healing.
  Primary teeth have a larger pulp chamber and thinner dentin walls than permanent teeth.
  Primary teeth have a wider apex and a more open apical foramen, which allows for better blood supply and healing.
  Odontoblasts are cells that produce dentin, and they are more active in younger teeth.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.
Action: Answer("A")

Question: Arrange the sequence of auditory pathway from peripheral to central: Inferior colliculus Cochlear nucleus Auditory coex Medial geniculate body
Choices:
  A: B>A>D>C
  B: B>D>C>A
  C: A>D>B>C
  D: C>A>B>D
Response 0:
Thought:
  The auditory pathway starts from the ear and ends in the brain.
  The cochlear nucleus is the first structure in the auditory pathway that receives input from the ear.
  The inferior colliculus is the next structure in the pathway that receives input from the cochlear nucleus.
  The medial geniculate body is the final structure in the pathway that receives input from the inferior colliculus.
  The auditory cortex is the final destination of the auditory pathway.
  Therefore, the correct sequence of auditory pathway from peripheral to central is Cochlear nucleus (B) > Inferior colliculus (A) > Medial geniculate body (D) > Auditory cortex (C).
  The answer is A: B>A>D>C.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The auditory pathway starts from the ear and ends in the brain.
  The cochlear nucleus is the first structure in the auditory pathway that receives input from the ear.
  The auditory nerve fibers synapse in the cochlear nucleus, which then sends the signal to the superior olivary nucleus.
  The superior olivary nucleus sends the signal to the inferior colliculus, which is located in the midbrain.
  From the inferior colliculus, the signal is sent to the medial geniculate body, which is located in the thalamus.
  Finally, the signal is sent to the auditory cortex in the temporal lobe of the brain.
  Therefore, the correct sequence of the auditory pathway from peripheral to central is: Cochlear nucleus > Superior olivary nucleus > Inferior colliculus > Medial geniculate body.
  The answer is B: B>D>C>A.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure used to access the root of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the root surface has been exposed for 6 years.
  PDL fibres are attached to cementum, not dentin.
  Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface is a common finding.
  Co adaptation to the remaining fibres is not a clear outcome of the procedure.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical technique used to access the root of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means the root surface has been exposed for 6 years.
  The periodontal ligament (PDL) fibres attach the tooth to the surrounding bone.
  The cementum is the layer of tissue that covers the root surface of the tooth.
  Dentin is the layer of tissue that makes up the bulk of the tooth.
  Epithelium is a layer of cells that covers the surface of the body.
  Co adaptation is the process of adapting to a new situation.
  Given that the root surface has been denuded for 6 years, the PDL fibres are likely to have been lost.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
Action: Answer("C")

Topic: Biochemistry
Question: Which of the following has least density?
Choices:
  A: VLDL
  B: LDL
  C: HDL
  D: Chylomicrons
Response 0:
Thought:
  Density is inversely proportional to size of lipoproteins.
  Chylomicrons are the largest lipoproteins.
  VLDL (Very Low Density Lipoprotein) is smaller than chylomicrons but larger than LDL and HDL.
  LDL (Low Density Lipoprotein) is smaller than VLDL but larger than HDL.
  HDL (High Density Lipoprotein) is the smallest lipoprotein.
  Therefore, HDL has the least density.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  VLDL, LDL, HDL, and chylomicrons are all lipoproteins.
  Lipoproteins are classified based on their density.
  The higher the protein content, the higher the density.
  Chylomicrons have the least protein content, and hence the least density.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Chylomicrons.

Question: A primigravida came to the labor room at 40 weeks + 5 days gestation for induction of labor. On per vaginal examination, the cervix is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced. The veex is at --1 station and the cervix is soft and posterior. What will be the modified bishop score for this lady?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought:
  The Bishop score is used to assess the cervical readiness for induction of labor.
  The Bishop score includes five components: cervical dilation, cervical effacement, cervical consistency, cervical position, and fetal station.
  The maximum score is 13 and the minimum score is 0.
  In this case, the cervical dilation is 1 cm, the effacement is 30%, the consistency is soft, the position is posterior, and the fetal station is -1.
  Therefore, the modified Bishop score will be 0+1+1+0+1=3.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The Bishop Score is a system used to assess the readiness of the cervix for induction of labor.
  The score is based on five components: cervical dilation, cervical effacement, cervical consistency, cervical position, and fetal station.
  Each component is scored from 0 to 2, with a maximum possible score of 10.
  In this case, the cervical dilation is 1 cm, which scores 0 points.
  The cervical effacement is 30%, which scores 1 point.
  The cervical consistency is not mentioned, so we assume it is average, which scores 1 point.
  The cervical position is posterior, which scores 0 points.
  The fetal station is -1, which scores 2 points.
  Adding up the scores, we get 4 points.
  However, since this is a primigravida, we add 1 point to the total score, giving us a modified Bishop Score of 5.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 5.

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 45 of 100 ###
Topic: Dental
Question: Occurrence of malocclusion in given population is best described as:
Choices:
  A: Prevalence rate
  B: Incidence rate
  C: Morbidity
  D: Probability
Response 0:
Thought:
  Malocclusion is a condition where the teeth are not properly aligned.
  Prevalence rate refers to the proportion of individuals in a population with a particular condition at a specific point in time.
  Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a condition in a population over a specific period of time.
  Morbidity refers to the state of being diseased or unhealthy within a population.
  Probability refers to the likelihood of an event occurring.
  Since the question is asking about the proportion of individuals in a population with a particular condition, the best answer is A: Prevalence rate.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Malocclusion refers to the misalignment of teeth or jaws.
  Prevalence rate refers to the proportion of individuals in a population with a specific condition at a given time.
  Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a specific condition in a population over a specific time period.
  Morbidity refers to the state of being diseased or unhealthy.
  Probability refers to the likelihood of an event occurring.
  Malocclusion is a condition that is present in a population at a given time, rather than a new occurrence.
  Therefore, the best description of the occurrence of malocclusion in a given population is prevalence rate.

  Incidence rate is the number of new cases of a disease or condition in a population over a period of time.
  Morbidity is the state of being diseased or unhealthy within a population.
  Probability is the likelihood of an event occurring.
  Since malocclusion is a condition that affects a population over a period of time, the best description of its occurrence would be prevalence rate.

Topic: Pathology
Question: Iron entry into enterocytes occurs which of the following?
Choices:
  A: DMT-1
  B: Ferropoin
  C: Transferrin
  D: Hepcidin
Response 0:
Thought:
  Iron entry into enterocytes is the first step in iron absorption.
  DMT-1 is a transmembrane protein that facilitates iron uptake into enterocytes.
  Ferropoin is not involved in iron entry into enterocytes.
  Transferrin is an iron transport protein that carries iron in the blood.
  Hepcidin is a hormone that regulates iron metabolism and inhibits iron absorption.
  Therefore, the answer is A: DMT-1.

  A: Type 1
  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4

  Type 1 root canal system has a single canal that runs straight from the pulp chamber to the tip of the root.
  Type 2 root canal system has two canals that join into one canal before exiting the root.
  Type 3 root canal system has two canals that exit the root separately.
  Type 4 root canal system has multiple canals that exit the root separately.

Topic: Dental
Question: Looseness seen in a recently delivered RPD is due to:
Choices:
  A: Defective occlusal balancing
  B: Passive clasp on abutment
  C: Thin flange
  D: Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth
Response 0:
Thought:
  RPD stands for Removable Partial Denture.
  Looseness in RPD can be due to various reasons.
  Passive clasp on abutment means the clasp is not engaging the undercut on the abutment tooth.
  Thin flange means the part of the denture that extends into the vestibule is thin and flexible.
  Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth means the denture base is not covering enough of the posterior teeth.
  Defective occlusal balancing means the occlusion is not balanced and the forces are not distributed evenly.
  Among the given options, the most likely reason for looseness in RPD is Passive clasp on abutment.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  RPD stands for Removable Partial Denture.
  Looseness in RPD can be due to several reasons.
  Passive clasp on abutment is not a cause of looseness.
  Thin flange can cause discomfort but not looseness.
  Defective occlusal balancing can cause looseness in RPD.
  Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth can also cause looseness in RPD.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  RPD stands for Removable Partial Denture.
  Looseness in RPD can be due to various reasons.
  Passive clasp on abutment means the clasp is not engaging the tooth properly, which can cause looseness.
  Defective occlusal balancing means the denture is not balanced properly, which can cause discomfort and looseness.
  Thin flange means the part of the denture that rests on the gums is too thin, which can cause discomfort and looseness.

  B: Micrognathia
  C: Hypoglycemia
  D: Crowded teeth

  The tongue may also enlarge, leading to sleep apnea and difficulty speaking.

  Hypoglycemia is not a feature of acromegaly, but rather a complication of treatment with somatostatin analogs.

Choices:
  A: 20 mg
  B: 200 mg
  C: 300 mg
  D: 3000 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  Proteinuria is the presence of excess protein in the urine.
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy complication characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, often the kidneys.
  Severe preeclampsia is diagnosed when blood pressure is greater than 160/110 mm Hg and proteinuria is greater than or equal to 5 g in a 24-hour urine collection.
  5 g is equivalent to 5000 mg.
  Therefore, the answer is not A, B, or C.
  The correct answer is D: 3000 mg.

  According to the American College of Obstetricians and Gynecologists (ACOG), proteinuria is one of the criteria for the diagnosis of severe preeclampsia.
  ACOG defines severe preeclampsia as having a blood pressure of 160/110 mm Hg or higher and proteinuria of 5 g or more in a 24-hour urine specimen or a urine protein-to-creatinine ratio of 0.5 or more.

Choices:
  A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis
  B: Giant cell tumor
  C: Chondroblastoma
  D: Osteoid osteoma
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient is a 9-year-old boy presenting with a lytic lesion on the midshaft tibia.
  On HPE, there are grooved nuclei, giant cells, eosinophilic cytoplasm, and fibroblastic proliferation.
  X-ray shows a lytic lesion with cortical thinning and expansion.
  Langerhans cell histiocytosis, also known as eosinophilic granuloma, is a rare disease that can cause bone lesions in children.
  Giant cell tumor is a benign bone tumor that can occur in the epiphysis of long bones and is more common in adults.
  Chondroblastoma is a rare benign tumor that occurs in the epiphysis of long bones and is more common in children and young adults.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign bone tumor that occurs in the cortex of long bones and is more common in children and young adults.
  The patient's age, location of the lesion, and histopathological findings suggest that the likely diagnosis is A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis.
Action: Answer("A")

Question: In lead poisoning, there is an inhibition of some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway. This is reflected by the accumulation of what substance in blood?
Choices:
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III
  B: Ferrochelatase
  C: Porphob I inogen
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid
Response 0:
Thought:
  The heme biosynthetic pathway is responsible for the production of heme, which is a component of hemoglobin.
  Lead poisoning inhibits some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Accumulation of what substance in blood reflects this inhibition?
  Uroporphyrinogen III and coproporphyrinogen III accumulate in congenital porphyrias.
  Ferrochelatase is the last enzyme in the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Porphobinogen is a precursor of heme and is not a final product.
  Delta-aminolevulinic acid (ALA) is the first product of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Inhibition of ALA dehydratase by lead results in the accumulation of ALA.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Delta amino levulinic acid.

Question: A 70 years old hypeensive patient with stage 5 chronic kidney disease was diagnosed recently with Type 2 diabetes mellitus. He doesn't want to take injectable insulin. Which of the following oral hypoglycemic agents will be preferred in this patient, which won't require any renal dose modification?
Choices:
  A: Linagliptin
  B: Repaglinide
  C: Vildagliptin
  D: Glimepiride
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient has stage 5 chronic kidney disease, which means the kidneys are functioning at less than 15% of normal capacity.
  In such patients, the use of metformin is contraindicated due to the risk of lactic acidosis.
  Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea, which is metabolized by the liver and excreted by the kidneys.
  Repaglinide is metabolized by the liver and excreted by the biliary system.
  Linagliptin and Vildagliptin are dipeptidyl peptidase-4 (DPP-4) inhibitors, which are not metabolized by the liver or excreted by the kidneys.
  Therefore, the preferred oral hypoglycemic agent in this patient would be a DPP-4 inhibitor.
  Among the given options, Linagliptin and Vildagliptin are DPP-4 inhibitors.
  However, Vildagliptin is not available in the United States.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Linagliptin.
Action: Answer("A")

  Repaglinide, Vildagliptin, and Glimepiride are primarily eliminated by the kidneys, so their dose should be adjusted in renal impairment.
  Therefore, Linagliptin will be preferred in this patient.

Question: Which of the following is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results?
Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Thought:
  Systematic random sampling is a type of probability sampling where every nth element is selected from a list.
  Simple random sampling is a type of probability sampling where every individual in a population has an equal chance of being selected.
  Stratified random sampling is a type of probability sampling where the population is divided into subgroups and individuals are randomly selected from each subgroup.
  Cluster sampling is a type of probability sampling where the population is divided into clusters and entire clusters are randomly selected.
  The question is asking about selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
  Stratified random sampling is used when the population is divided into subgroups based on potential factors that will affect the results.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.
Action: Answer("C")

- Cluster sampling is a method where groups or clusters are selected randomly and all individuals within the selected clusters are included in the study.
- The question is asking about selecting patients based on potential factors that will affect the results.
- Stratified random sampling is a method that is commonly used to select patients based on specific factors.

  A: Functional class III
  B: Class I type I
  C: Class II div I
  D: Class II div II

  Familial inheritance refers to the genetic transmission of a trait from parent to offspring.
  Strong familial inheritance means that the trait is highly likely to be passed down from generation to generation.

  Other abnormalities may include hepatosplenomegaly, thrombocytopenia, and chorioretinitis.
